Wuxi Chamber of Commerce's Opinion on Holding Business Registration 64

List Six Research Points

Cable All County Chambers of Commerce to Adopt

The Jiangsu Provincial Government held a business tax and specially convened representatives from various county chambers of commerce the other day, and Ren Zhen held a meeting to discuss the measures. It was decided to change the business registration and collect the registration fee as a transitional measure, and provisional regulations were formulated. Cheng Jingtang, the representative sent by the Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce to the provincial meeting, has returned to Wuxi and reported the results of the meeting. The association has specifically listed six research points on the issue of business registration in Jiangsu Province and sent a telegram to the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce, requesting that the chambers of commerce of various counties earnestly study them. The text of the telegram is recorded below: 1. All the members of the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce and the chambers of commerce of all the counties, the telegrams have been sent, the Jiangsu Province business tax meeting, and the results of the report by the representative of our association. The change of business registration and the collection of registration fees, Chen, the director of the Finance Department, delivered an opening speech and stated that the provincial government had long had the determination to abolish the likin, and this transitional measure was to change the business tax after the future abolition of the likin. The method is extremely simple, the donation rate is based on the capital, and merchants are allowed to report it themselves. No other collection agency will be set up, and the financial bureaus of various counties will be entrusted to handle it concurrently. It can be seen that the government is considerate of the people's hardships and is meticulous in every possible way. It is found that business registration was decided by the Ministry of Finance's likin abolition meeting in the Republic of China in 1928. The first article of the general outline of the measures for collecting business tax in various provinces lists the matters clearly, which is similar to the fourth article of the temporary regulations on business license donation originally formulated by Jiangsu Province this time. However, the second item clearly states that no license fee will be charged for business licenses. It seems that there is no provision for the collection of registration fees. However, since the provincial government has sincerely encouraged it to alleviate the current financial difficulties of Jiangsu Province, how dare businessmen and the people not share the difficulties together, in order to live up to the Constitution. However, since it is based on the premise of preparing for the business tax, all measures should still be based on the general outline of the measures for collecting business tax in various provinces decided by the Ministry of Finance's likin abolition meeting in 1928. There are several matters that should be carefully studied: 1. The original plan for the business registration fee is to collect 1/1000 to 2/1000 of the capital. It seems that the business tax rate is stipulated in Article 2 of the original method, but the second item of the same article also has the types and conditions of the business. If there are special circumstances in each province, it may formulate its own flexible measures and tax standards and report them to the Ministry of Finance for approval and implementation. However, the tax rate levied shall not be higher than the provisions of this outline. Is it appropriate to collect a kind of handling fee at the highest business tax rate? This should be researched. 2. The collection of the business tax registration fee is a transition for the business tax. If the business tax is levied again in the future, according to Article 1, Item 2 of the original method, the license must be renewed once a year. Is it still necessary to collect the registration fee? This should be researched. 3. Director Chen of the Finance Department stated in his opening speech that the donation rate is based on capital and merchants are allowed to report it themselves. However, Article 6 of the temporary regulations stipulates that the collection agency shall send personnel to investigate the amount of capital once a year. When deemed necessary, it may check various covenants, contracts, and account books. Article 11 of the implementation rules stipulates that the county bureaus shall send investigators to various townships in the winter of each year to investigate the business situation and the increase or decrease of capital in order to rectify the amount of donations. Will there be any disputes in the future? This should be researched. 4. Article 3 of the original method stipulates that if the business tax is overdue, an additional 10% will be charged for each month that it is overdue, up to 30%. However, Article 11 of the temporary regulations originally formulated by Jiangsu Province stipulates that anyone who operates without a license, or conceals capital and underreports it, shall be ordered to pay the amount in full after being found out, and shall be fined one time the amount that should be paid. It seems that the penalty rules are heavier than the original method. This should be researched. 5. Article 5 of the original method stipulates that a business tax review committee shall be established to be filled by collection officials, members of the chamber of commerce, and accountants. However, Article 7 of the implementation rules of the temporary regulations originally formulated by Jiangsu Province stipulates that the county bureaus shall invite the chairman of the chamber of commerce as a consultant to assist in all matters when handling business license donations. It seems that it is not as appropriate as establishing a review committee according to the original method. This should be researched. 6. Business tax is local income and is recorded in Article 1 of the original method, but there is a difference between local provinces and counties, and the county local fees are also difficult. If it is necessary to follow suit in the future, it is not what merchants and the people can afford. Should there be a clear indication of restrictions or prior proper allocation to avoid repeated burdens on merchants and the people? This should be researched. In short, the collection of business registration fees in Jiangsu Province is a transition for preparing the business tax. If the planning is not thorough, it will be an obstacle to the future business tax. It seems that both officials and the people should conduct thorough research to promote the benefits as much as possible, so as not to live up to the meaning of the current government's diligence in seeking the people's sentiments and broad consultation. Our association's views are exhausted, and we dare not spare our foolishness, so we specially send a telegram to report it. I hope you will adopt it and look forward to your public view. Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce Jiang.

Execution of Bandits: Hou A'bao, a native of Dachang, 24 years old, last November, colluded with a group of people to rob the home of Zhu Pinquan, a resident of Mengjiaqiao, Nanxiang, and shot and killed the victim on the spot. He escaped without a trace. He was later arrested by the county government, and after a clear interrogation, he was sentenced to death and reported to the High Court. Zhang, the trial judge, took the prisoner out of prison at noon to verify his identity and escorted him to a mound near Gaosheng Bridge outside the West Gate for execution by shooting.

Prisoners Commit Crimes and Extort Money: The prisoners Chen Gentao, Tang Haoran, Wang Shenglin, Li Linggen, etc. are extremely cunning and fierce. They extort money from new prisoners. Songjiang 66

County Government Meeting Minutes: The County Government held its 77th County Government Meeting yesterday, chaired by County Magistrate Jin. Matters discussed: (1) Regarding the Conghua Pavilion County Bridge, since the reconstruction of the Ping Bridge, the passage of ships has been excessively impeded by the bridge surface, making passage difficult. (2) Regarding the order from the Civil Affairs Department in April of this year, requiring all county organs to submit their budget resolutions for review by the County Government Meeting in accordance with Article 22 of the County Organization Law, and the order from the Finance Department to issue budget forms up to the 19th fiscal year, which had been prepared and sent by the Finance Bureau but had not been officially approved. Suzhou 67

Gang Leader Arrested in Suzhou: Xia Jinrong, the leader of the Henan gang in Taihu Lake, also known as Xia Da, repeatedly colluded with other gang leaders such as Tian Pangzi and Mao Zilong to rob Wuzhen, Zhejiang Province, last winter. In February of this year, he robbed the Shenhu small ferry boat, kidnapped people, and killed them. This spring, during the suppression of bandits by the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Water Police, he killed Li Guobin, the captain of the Third District Guerrilla Team in Suzhou, and wounded Xu Pucheng, the head of the Third District in Zhejiang. He has committed numerous crimes and has been on the run. Recently, he was found hiding in Suzhou. On the night before yesterday (the 3rd), Cai Jun and Liu Hongkui, two detectives from the Zhejiang Water Police, came to Suzhou and arrested Xia Jinrong and his wife at Room 6 of the Sanxin Inn outside the gate. They were sent to the Public Security Bureau for detention. A telephone report was made to the Third District of the Zhejiang Water Police in Jiaxing. Yesterday (the 4th), the Zhejiang Third District dispatched the Zhiguo warship to Suzhou and took Xia and his wife back to Zhejiang to face justice.

Temporary Bandit Suppression Command Headquarters Abolished: The Three-Province Bandit Suppression Headquarters, due to the bandit leader Taibao Ashu and his gang disturbing Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, specially appointed Hu Zhengji as the Temporary Commander for Bandit Suppression in Songjiang, Qingpu, Jinshan, and Pinghu counties. The Wuxian County Water and Land Police Force was also placed under Hu's command. Now that Taibao Ashu's bandit gang has been repeatedly suppressed by the Jiangsu and Zhejiang water and land military police, their strength has been completely lost, and they have dispersed into the villages in the Jinshan and Pinghu areas, hiding their weapons to avoid the attention of the authorities. Commander Hu, after receiving reports, believed that the ongoing village cleansing in various counties was sufficient to eliminate the remaining bandits, so he reported to the Headquarters to temporarily abolish the Temporary Command Headquarters. The regiment was ordered to send a company of soldiers to Jinshan and Pinghu counties to assist in the village cleansing. Commander Xiong, based on this, notified the County Government yesterday for information.

Crackdown on Refugees Heading South: After the Huang County Magistrate reported to the Civil Affairs Department for instructions on how to eliminate the concerns about the harassment and plundering of property by more than 400 refugees from Hunan in Yinshan Town, an order was received yesterday to have each water police chief work together to prevent the problem. A report was also sent to the Provincial Government, informing neighboring provinces to stop the refugees from leaving their province, and issuing orders to the counties north of the river to follow the previous orders and crack down on refugees heading south to cut off the source.

Painter Falls to Death: To widen Guanqian Street, shops are demolishing and rebuilding inward together. As the Mid-Autumn Festival is approaching and winter goods are about to be marketed, the contractor is urged to speed up the work. Although the buildings of the Dadong Factory on Guanxi Main Street have been completed, the interior painting has not yet been finished, so Yin Shunyu Paint Shop was hired to handle it. Yesterday (the 4th) morning at about 8:00 AM, the paint shop ordered worker Xu Ada to go to paint, standing under the ceiling of the three-story building. He accidentally lost his footing and fell, landing on the Shuimen River. He lost consciousness and was barely breathing. The workers carried him to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but he died before reaching the hospital. It's truly tragic.

Wuxi 68

Dies of Anxiety Over Huge Losses: Zhu Chunshan, the owner of the Zhu Chunji Rice Shop in Nanshi, Shanghai, 55 years old, recently took a car to Nanjing with his son to collect debts totaling more than 5,000 yuan as the lunar Mid-Autumn Festival was approaching. After arriving in Beijing, the debtor had already disappeared. Zhu Chunshan was extremely anxious as he could not collect the debts and burst into tears. His son accompanied him by car to Wuxi to visit his relative Wang Ziming, north of the North Gate, at Nanguang's house for a temporary rest. Zhu Chunshan was old and weak and could not bear the anxiety, and he died of exhaustion yesterday (4th) at dawn. His son urgently telegraphed Shanghai to inform his mother to come to Wuxi to handle the funeral. It is truly tragic.

Minutes of the Joint Meeting of Silk Factories: The Wuxi Silk Factory Association convened a meeting in opposition to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau's implementation of public measurement and inspection, and a resolution was unanimously passed against it. It is now learned that the association convened its fourth joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members yesterday afternoon at about 2:00 PM. More than ten committee members, including Zhong Fenghao, Yang Yuchu, and Xue Shouxuan, attended. Chairman Qian Fenghao reported the purpose of the meeting and then began discussions. The resolved matters are as follows: (1) Regarding the recent shutdown of some silk factories in Shanghai, it was proposed to request government funding to maintain operations. It was resolved that the Wuxi industry should unite with Shanghai and jointly make the request. (2) The China General Federation of Industry and the China Industrial and Commercial Management Committee sent letters soliciting members. It was resolved to nominate Qian Fenghao as a member. (3) Regarding whether to suspend operations in Wuxi to oppose public measurement and inspection, it was resolved that because this matter is of great importance, a general membership meeting would be convened on the 5th of this month to resolve it.

Changzhou 69

Militia Police Massacre Villagers While Suppressing Bandits: An exchange of fire between police and bandits occurred in Huangcun Town on the border of Jiangyin the day before yesterday. The bandits fled toward Baizhang Xutang in Wujin. At about 4:00 AM on the 3rd, Liu Zaigeng, the head of the Sixth District of the county, led over a hundred armed militia police and plainclothes officers to surround Baizhang Town. First, they disarmed the town's security force and placed six members under guard, then searched the suspected Nanjie shops. It was then learned that the Fushengxiang Beijing goods shop was suspected of harboring bandits, so they broke down the door. The shop owner, Peng Jinkang, was the head of Changshou Township. His younger brother, Peng Quanlin, lived behind the shop. The militia police opened the door to Peng Quanlin's room, dragged Quanlin out of bed naked to the door, and shot him, killing him instantly. Then, they used a kitchen knife to cut off Quanlin's head and took it away. Over twenty people from various shops, including Liu Mengqing, were arrested. Farmer Song Jingru was also hit by a stray bullet near the ear. Those arrested and Peng Quanlin's head were taken to Huangtu Town. After an interrogation, the head was sent back, and the suspects were released on bail. Among them, Jin Shougen, Han Genda, and Liu Yulin were to be sent to Jiangyin for interrogation. Cheng Foyu, the head of the Fourth District of Wujin County, reported the aforementioned situation upon hearing the news and immediately telegraphed the County Government and the County Court, stating that Peng Quanlin was neither a bandit nor a villain and that this massacre was too cruel to bear. The County Government then dispatched Police Squad Captain Jiang Bingkun to lead a team to investigate, and the County Court Supervisory Prosecutor led officials to conduct a post-mortem examination on the morning of the 4th.

Special Feature

Opinions on Tax Revenue Policies of the Committee Designed by Gamal of the Ministry of Finance (Continued) 77

Now let us discuss the position of indirect taxes in China's tax system. Regarding stamp duty, the committee has thoroughly discussed it in the draft stamp duty law and its explanatory memorandum submitted on January 18, 1929. Apart from this, there are indirect taxes on goods.

At present, the national government's revenue largely depends on customs duties, especially import duties. From the perspective of the situation, this tax revenue will still be a major financial source for China's reliance in the years to come. Generally speaking, old taxes are easier to collect than new taxes. Customs duties have long been regarded as part of China's tax system, so their collection is easier than that of new taxes. Moreover, because customs duties are relatively unaffected by political turmoil, their administrative efficiency is greater than that of general inland tax administration. For all these reasons, if careful consideration is given when formulating tax regulations, it will be easier to increase revenue from customs import duties than from other tax sources. From an administrative point of view, China's tax revenue should rely on import customs duties. However, other aspects should also be considered, especially the burden of taxation. What impact does the imposition of import duties on goods used by the poorer classes have on the prices of goods? This is a question that we cannot but study. Here is a brief discussion of this topic:

Most of the imported goods used by the poorer classes in China are cotton fabrics, kerosene, cigarettes, matches, light wood, and needles. The average annual value of these goods imported from foreign countries between 1925 and 1928 was 353,000,000 taels of customs silver, accounting for one-third of the total imports. Although this amount does not fully represent the burden of customs duties on the poor, if the increase in tax rates can be limited to imported goods other than the above, and appropriate regulations are made on the tax rates levied, then the tax revenue from imported goods will be greater than that currently collected. On the one hand, the burden on the poor will be avoided from being significantly increased, and on the other hand, no class will be unduly burdened.

There is considerable reason to believe that customs import duties will not unduly burden the poor. There is also no doubt that other parts of China's tax system are sufficient to unduly burden the poor. Let us first talk about the salt tax:

Salt is a necessity of life. Regardless of whether they are poor or rich, the amount they consume does not vary much. Moreover, the handling of salt tax collection is not appropriate. Even if the handling is appropriate, the amount of tax paid by each person will definitely not differ according to each person's ability to pay taxes. The people's economic capacity should be the standard for paying taxes, but in fact, it is the opposite. In other words, this kind of tax that is light on the rich and heavy on the poor is an unfair tax. Although various commodity taxes somewhat contain this kind of unfairness, it is especially obvious when this kind of tax is imposed on daily necessities such as salt. In addition, the regular customs duties, re-import duties, and taxes on goods traveling between various ports in China have the same situation.

Since this tax has the effect of unduly burdening the poor, when formulating the tax system, efforts should be made to eliminate this kind of unfair tax. This is not only a wise policy, but also deeply in line with humanitarianism.

Based on these reasons, this committee specifically recommends the collection of consumption taxes on matches and cement. The taxation of these kinds of goods is indeed stipulated in the special consumption tax regulations. However, this committee recommends that the aforementioned two kinds of flowage taxes not be collected directly from consumers, but from producers. The reason why this kind of tax is called a consumption tax is that this tax money is usually added to the price of the goods, so that the person paying the tax is the person consuming the goods.

There are several points in the current special consumption tax regulations that are questionable. These regulations include a wide range of taxable goods, making it impossible to estimate the possible impact of this kind of tax on society. Even regarding the determination of the tax rate and the selection of taxable goods, it seems that the possible impact on industry has not been given due consideration. Often, the same goods are taxed repeatedly during various stages of their manufacture. Therefore, in order to avoid double taxation, there must be complicated regulations regarding tax refunds. In general, the implementation of any tax must pay attention to the scope and possible impact of this tax, and attention must also be paid to avoiding tax overlap. Other aspects, such as the selection of taxable goods, whether the tax rate is appropriate, whether the administrative organization is effective, and whether it is economical, and whether the administrative methods are suitable for the special conditions of industry, should all be studied. This committee's draft special consumption tax law on cement and the special consumption tax law on matches are believed to be in line with the aforementioned tax requirements. (To be continued)

Seamen's Wage Increase Movement 84

The Stance of Six Foreign Shipping Companies

Three Methods Determined

Recently, seamen have been negotiating with foreign shipping companies such as Taikoo and Jardine Matheson regarding wage increases, but no resolution has been reached. This matter has been reported in this newspaper several times. After investigation, this matter has causes and consequences. The seamen's demands are extremely legitimate. Yesterday, the reporter specially visited Tang Hesheng and others, the standing committee members of the Shanghai branch of the Seamen's Industrial Union, to inquire about the progress of this matter. They provided a detailed account of the process and current steps, which are recorded below.

The Motivation for Wage Increases: Seamen first proposed the demand for wage increases in the spring of last year, referring to the wages of the stokers, sailors, and stewards on the river and sea vessels. They requested a reasonable increase, as seamen's wages were already very low and had not been increased for ten years. During the tenth year of the Republic, the Seamen's Union in Hong Kong made a wage increase request to British shipowners, stipulating that seamen's wages should be increased every three years. However, more than ten years have passed, and the shipowners have not fulfilled this agreement. Last spring, after the seamen's request for wage increases was drafted, it was painfully suspended due to the ongoing campaign against the rebels, fearing that it would be disrupted by reactionaries and hinder the current situation. This year, due to the sharp rise in the cost of living, seamen were forced to make demands to the shipping companies.

Chinese Ships Agree to Increase: After the Seamen's Union proposed the wage increase request this year, Yu Qiaqing, Chen Bogang, Chen Ganqing, and other members of the Shanghai Shipping Association invited representatives of the seamen and representatives of various Chinese shipping companies to a meeting for discussion. It was agreed to cancel the previously provided rice allowance and increase the wages of each seaman by six yuan, starting with four yuan in August of this year and an additional two yuan starting in March of next year. At that time, the seamen also expressed their agreement, and the Shipping Association informed all Chinese shipping companies in the association to implement the agreed wage increase plan.

Negotiations with Six Foreign Ships: The foreign shipping companies in this port that operate on the river and sea routes and employ Chinese seamen include six companies: British Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Asia, American Jiejiang, Mobil, and Japanese Nisshin. There are more Chinese ships than foreign ships. Since the Seamen's Union made the wage increase request, it made the same request to the six foreign shipping companies. When the Chinese ships agreed to increase, the six foreign shipping companies still made no response. Because they are not members of the Shipping Association, the Seamen's Union had to negotiate with each of these companies separately. Nisshin, Mobil, Asia, and Jiejiang all claimed that if Taikoo and Jardine Matheson agreed to increase, they would also grant the increase according to the precedent.

The Stance of Foreign Merchants: After receiving the request from the Seamen's Union, the British Taikoo Company had several discussions with representatives of the union. First, it wanted to invite members of the Shanghai Shipping Association to mediate, but because it was not a member of the association, it was not convenient to proceed. Therefore, the union negotiated directly. After many consultations, Taikoo Company only agreed to cancel the two yuan rice allowance that it had automatically added in June and increase the wages of each person by three yuan. However, the seamen also had to add six yuan according to the increase promised by the Chinese ships. Now, only half of the amount is allowed, which is too far from the proposed amount, and the negotiations have not yielded results.

Steps to Proceed: Yesterday, the Seamen's Union originally planned to hold a meeting at 9 AM to discuss methods to deal with the wage increase requests to the various foreign shipping companies. However, because the members could not arrive on time, the meeting could not be held. Now, the union has already agreed on two methods to proceed: (1) Dispatch representatives to contact the six foreign shipping companies again to request: (A) First increase wages by six yuan, (B) Then increase wages once every five years. (2) The Seamen's Union will detail the negotiation process and the firm refusal of various foreign ships to increase wages and submit it to the Central Party Department, requesting the government to provide assistance as soon as possible to urge foreign shipowners to fulfill the wage increase conditions as soon as possible and resolve the case as soon as possible. (3) When negotiations break down and there is no other choice, the final countermeasure can only be implemented. However, if there is hope of compromise, they are determined not to adopt the breakup method.

Fifth Day of the National Anti-Drug Week 88

Disaster Relief Day Today is the Disaster Relief Day of the seventh National Anti-Drug Campaign Week. The health campaign of the other day has been reported in the previous newspaper. The following is a summary of the Disaster Relief Day campaign:

Disaster Relief Day Measures 89

(A) Significance: The reason why our country has been plagued by famine and widespread disasters throughout history is ultimately due to the increasingly severe scourge of drugs. After intimidation and enticement, ignorant farmers have no choice but to plant opium, which reduces the amount of rice and food supply, leading to famine. If we do not seek remedies quickly, the crisis will appear immediately. Compatriots, how can we not wake up! (B) Purpose: The purpose of the Disaster Relief Day of this Anti-Drug Week is to awaken compatriots, understand the causes of famine in our country, unite to eliminate the drug demon, save millions of dying disaster victims, and restore the national spirit of our country. (C) Measures: (1) Implement rural education, (2) Investigate the actual situation in disaster areas caused by opium cultivation, (3) Organize anti-drug and disaster relief propaganda teams, (4) Hold anti-drug lectures and propaganda by the education party.

Outline of Propaganda for Disaster Relief Day 90

Facts tell us that the fertilizer for growing opium consumes more than that for growing ordinary crops because its absorption is very large. Most farmers are very economical, and they are willing to provide as much as possible for the needs of opium. As a result, the original nourishment of the land for growing opium is gradually absorbed by it invisibly. That is, the "power of the soil" as the saying goes. Fertile land gradually becomes barren and weak. Therefore, if you change to growing other crops for one year, its production will naturally be reduced compared to land that has not grown opium. As a result, land that has been continuously planted with opium for several years will naturally be reduced. In general, if you change to growing crops with artificial fertilizer, how can it grow and harvest? This is the relationship between growing opium and soil deterioration. Gansu and Shaanxi provinces cannot transport heavy timber to foreign countries for resale due to inconvenient transportation, so they grow opium. Because opium is small in size and valuable, it is much lighter and more convenient than timber. The authorities strictly prohibit opium in order to regulate the province's finances. However, we think that if the transportation of heavy timber is impossible in Gansu due to inconvenient transportation, can heavy food be transported in? If food cannot be transported in, then it should be planted in its own place. Barley, evening primrose, millet, and beans are all important food crops in the north. Why don't they grow these crops and instead grow opium? Although opium is small in size, valuable, and easy to transport, no matter how much money you accumulate, you cannot survive if you cannot transport food. It is a suicidal policy to covet small profits and abandon people's lives. The situation in Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou is similar. A few years ago, there was a great famine in Sichuan, Guizhou, and Yunnan provinces. The Chinese and foreign charity organizations said that in the past, as long as there was money, food could be obtained everywhere. Now, real food must be transported to provide relief. The famine in Henan, Gansu, and Shaanxi last year was also the same phenomenon. It can be seen that growing opium does reduce food production, which not only affects the province but also affects the whole country. This is the relationship between growing opium and the lack of food, which leads to famine. According to our field survey of twenty opium-growing farmers, fifteen families like to grow opium and five families do not like to grow opium. It can be seen that most villagers also like to grow opium. The reason why they like to grow opium is because they covet high profits and steal opium taxes. If you carefully calculate it, you will lose money if you grow opium. They really didn't notice this. According to our field survey of thirty-seven farmers in Mengcheng Township, Anhui, the average cost of growing opium per acre is 32 yuan and 34 cents (including the cost of opium seedlings). The income per acre is only 23 yuan and 99 cents. As a result, you will lose 9 yuan and 35 cents per acre. Therefore, if you remove the opium seedlings, you will lose 9 yuan and 35 cents per acre. Therefore, you cannot avoid the cost of opium seedlings, and no one will not lose money if you grow opium. How important is the impact on farmers' livelihoods! This is the relationship between growing opium and farmers' livelihoods. From the above, we can know that although the famines in various places seem to be caused by unexpected floods and droughts, in fact, the lack of food has long been felt. However, it is becoming more and more obvious due to floods and droughts. Farmers are influenced by opium cultivation, are tempted by bandits, and join the ranks of bandits, resulting in bandits filling the area. In addition to the military affairs that have been fought for revolution in recent years, the prolongation of the civil war and the conflict of Sheng mostly stem from the competition for opium tax collection. In this way, flood drought soldiers, the planting of opium is actually the main reason. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association leads the country to hold the seventh Anti-Drug Campaign Week and specifically holds a day as Anti-Drug Disaster Relief Day to arouse the attention of the people across the country. Anti-drug comrades, we should thoroughly realize the various bad effects and bad consequences of planting opium. Taking advantage of this campaign day, on the one hand, we must educate and propagate that not growing opium is the fundamental way to relieve disasters. On the other hand, we must urge the authorities to strictly prohibit opium cultivation as the only way to thoroughly reject drugs. Our steps are: on the side of the people, conduct field surveys of the amount of opium planted in farmland and the lives of farmers, and study the improvement of the soil after opium cultivation and the alternative crops for opium cultivation; on the government side, petition the government authorities to strictly prohibit opium cultivation, eradicate opium seedlings, abolish opium seedling tax, and punish the corrupt officials who collect opium tax.

Investigation Plan on Opium Cultivation in Various Provinces 91

Based on the recent reports from anti-drug bodies across the country, according to reports from anti-drug comrades across the country, opium seedlings are still being planted and opium taxes and fines are being collected in Rehe, Liaoning, Sichuan, Yunnan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Guizhou, Henan, and northern Anhui, the same as before. Moreover, they are mostly forced to plant, not voluntarily planted by farmers. The famine has been going on for years, and the reason is actually planting here. The association has decided to conduct a nationwide investigation after the Anti-Drug Week to reduce disasters. It is reported that the main points of the investigation are as follows: (1) Whether the opium area has been effectively eradicated, (2) Whether there is any forced planting and tax collection by the military, (3) The living conditions of farmers, (4) Other crops suitable for converting opium fields.

News of Anti-Drug Activities in Mosques 92

The Christian churches in this city have always been enthusiastic about anti-drug activities. The Anti-Drug Association has asked them to support them unanimously. It is reported that all churches have expressed their sympathy for this Anti-Drug Campaign Week and will convene church members today to hold anti-drug worship. The association will distribute various colored pictures, slogans, propaganda outlines, and pledge forms for posting. All contacted churches have been notified by special letter, saying that members will be sent to the church to bring propaganda materials in advance. Please assist in posting them and give anti-drug speeches on the 5th Sunday of Worship, as well as solicit donations to assist our association in promoting anti-drug education and anti-smoking business. Please also let us know the progress.

Church Campaign Measures 93

In addition to issuing notices, the association has also formulated the measures for the church to hold the campaign, stating that all members of our church should do their duty. If there are teachers, they should do their best to promote God's justice and holiness so that soil traffickers and opium merchants can reform themselves. If believers, they should resolve to reject drugs and participate in persuading others to break away from opium. If we work together with one heart and one mind, success can be expected. Church groups and individuals should participate directly in anti-drug activities at any time and any place and work hard to promote them. During this Anti-Drug Week, they should also (1) hold anti-drug speeches to publicize the harm of opium, (2) investigate and report on the planting of drugs to the Anti-Drug Association, (3) promote the anti-smoking business and save addicts, (4) pray for the anti-smoking work and anti-drug campaign, (5) especially collect donations to support the anti-drug campaign. Today's special fundraising income will be used to fund the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association.

Declaration Urging Strict Enforcement of Opium Prohibition 94

The disaster of opium will lead to the destruction of the country. The harm is so terrible that it is beyond description. Since the National Government was established in Nanjing, it has repeatedly announced the prohibition in accordance with public opinion. At this time of national poverty, it is truly a good policy to save the country. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's last words show us that the opium business cannot coexist with a national government that grants power to the people. The Kuomintang platform also clearly stipulates the harm of opium. Prohibition is the responsibility of the authorities to Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the party, the country, and the people. No research or elaboration is needed. Without effective opium prohibition, there will be no way to face the party and the country, and no way to face public opinion. However, the situation of opium prohibition's neglect in recent years is truly heartbreaking. Opium poppies are all over Sichuan, Guizhou, Yunnan, and Shaanxi, which can be attributed to the control of warlords or excused by the unrest in the local area. But what about Fujian and Anhui? The Anhui garrison is directly under the central government, and the Fujian navy is under the Ministry of the Navy. Opium seedlings are planted and ignored, or there are those who take the opportunity to profit from it. People complain, and public opinion is boiling, but the collection of taxes by the garrison has not stopped. The special tax in the two lakes was originally a temporary measure to clear the surplus of Wuhan's native opium and show compassion. Native opium merchants are already illegal, but now the situation has changed and is becoming more and more serious. The Ministry of Finance sends members to set up groups, crack down on smuggling, and sell native opium publicly and transport it without any scruples. Native opium taxes and levies amount to millions. Wherever the corrupt government reaches, the darkness is rampant. Recently, there have been rumors of expanding it to the whole country, which has caused the world to laugh and the country's reputation to be lost. The people's opposition has not had the slightest effect. Since its establishment, the Anti-Opium Commission has been subject to restrictions in exercising its powers, and major native opium cases have not been investigated. This has disappointed the public and dissatisfied society. Other cases, such as strange ships transporting native opium and spreading rumors in the League of Nations, have been safely transported into Shanghai after being leaked, showing the strictness of the protection and the greatness of the organization. The ancient saints said that when the upper and lower classes fight for profit, the country will be in danger. Today, the opium disaster in our country is due to the leased land in the concession and the relationship of foreigners. However, the source of the disaster is actually the sins of the Chinese people themselves. People must insult themselves before others insult them. The country must invade itself before others invade it. Today, our country is suffering from drug addiction to this extent, and there are still those who are willing to indulge in drugs in order to seek high profits. How can we accuse foreigners of harming us? Our association is entrusted by the people to eliminate drugs as its mission. Our hearts are in danger, and it is difficult to keep silent. Therefore, we have listed the facts and issued a declaration based on the main points of the resolution passed by the Shanghai Joint Conference of Various Groups of the Seventh National Anti-Drug Campaign Week on October 1. We hope that the National Government authorities will take strict measures to stop the cultivation of opium in various provinces, abolish the native opium tax in the two lakes, eliminate selfish feelings, and disregard interests. We must follow Dr. Sun Yat-sen's words that the declaration of war on opium must never be compromised. If we can do this, the people of the whole country will bless and support us, and the achievements of the public will be forever recorded in history. The world will admire them for ten thousand years. It is time to correct the chaos and turn weakness into strength. We offer these few words, hoping for your consideration. We do not have time to calculate whether you know our guilt or blame us. This is the declaration.

The Social Bureau's Draft of the New Calendar for the Twentieth Year is Completed 95

The calendar for the twentieth year has been innovated again... It is planned to hand it over to the publishing house for printing. Recently, some unscrupulous merchants have colluded with vagrants to print and sell discarded calendars and sell them along the streets in the concession. The municipal government has sent a document to the special district court, ordering the police department to investigate and prohibit them. The public security bureau has also sent inspectors to secretly investigate, and the police station has seized a large number of discarded calendars. The court has punished them. It has been reported in this newspaper. Now it is reported that the Social Bureau has also completed the compilation and printing of the calendar for the twentieth year. The content is more complete than the calendar for the nineteenth year, and the compilation has been greatly innovated. Various texts are attached to ensure that people from all over the world can use it. Because the Social Bureau believes that during the period of political tutelage, it is necessary to pay attention to the spirit of the rule of law and the common sense that the people should have. The editing starts from this point. The draft has been completed and is now submitted to the municipal government for review and printing. It is reported that the Social Bureau intends that the calendar for the twentieth year should be printed by the book industry and the ink-colored lithography industry. Otherwise, the municipal government will still fund the printing and distribution. If various merchants want to print tens of thousands of copies like the Sanyou Industrial Society did last year and distribute them to customers, as well as publish advertisements in the calendar in the hope of receiving great results, they can contact the bureau as soon as possible.

Local News Two

Yesterday Morning's Murder of a Wet Nurse in Taoyuan Village 100

▲ Sudden Attack by Thugs

▲ The Motive Seemed Not Robbery

▲ The Wet Nurse Cried Out Before Dying

▲ The Criminals Fled Immediately

At 8:45 yesterday morning, a murder occurred at No. 15, Taoyuan Village, Lane 1295, Route Lafayette, French Concession, where a wet nurse was shot dead by thugs. The detailed account of the incident is recorded below:

Refugees Come to Shanghai: No. 15, Taoyuan Village, Lane 1295, Route Lafayette, French Concession, is a standalone Western-style house. A Mr. Xi from Henan Province had rented the house. Half a month ago, Mr. Xi's family came to Shanghai to seek refuge and temporarily chose to reside here. It was only for a very brief period.

Family Situation: Currently residing in the Xi household are three women: Mrs. Xi Tang, the mistress of the house; a paternal aunt of Mr. Xi's; and Tang Yixiu, the wet nurse brought from Yu (Henan Province), also known as Tang Tang, 36 years old, from Dong'an, Yongzhou, Yu. Tang had been working in the Xi family for over six years and was well-liked by her employers. Therefore, when the employers came to Shanghai to seek refuge, they brought her along to serve them.

Sudden Arrival of Thugs: At approximately 8:45 yesterday morning, the entire Xi household had risen and finished washing up. The wet nurse, Tang, was in the kitchen organizing items when suddenly three thugs wearing Zhongshan suits and long robes, speaking with a northern accent, intruded through the back door. They saw Tang as if she were invisible and intended to head straight upstairs. When Tang saw this, she was about to ask questions when the thugs pulled out pistols, forbade her from making noise, left one to watch her, and herded the rest of the household into a corner.

Tragic Death of the Wet Nurse: At that time, two thugs held Mrs. Xi Tang hostage and ordered her to go upstairs. The wet nurse, Tang, was extremely frightened and cried out, causing the thug watching her to fire three shots at her. The bullets hit her left temple and head, and she immediately fell to the ground, lifeless and dead. The two thugs holding the mistress inspected the upstairs and, seeing no one, and hearing the gunshots downstairs, dared not linger. They went downstairs together and fled through the back door without a trace.

Corpse Examination and Coffin Preparation: After the incident, the Lou Ka Wan Police Station was notified and immediately dispatched Detective Hong Chunxiang, Zhang Ziying, and others to investigate the scene. They carried the body to the Tongren Fu Yuan Tang mortuary for an autopsy. Subsequently, the French Concession Police Criminal Division reported to the French Court Judge Zhu Cheng, who arrived at the mortuary at 11:30 a.m. He confirmed that the deceased had died from gunshot wounds sustained before death. He ordered photographs to be taken and instructed the employer to prepare a coffin for burial, while the police would strictly investigate and arrest the criminals for questioning.

Major Fire on Qiaojia Road 101

A Madman, Qian Yanxing, Burns to Death

▲ Opium Smoking Causes a Devastating Fire

▲ Twenty Houses Destroyed in Two Hours

▲ Madam Wang Chen and Her Daughters Injured in Falls

The resident at No. 189, Qiaojia Road, inside the Great South Gate of the city, at the corner of the Meijia Lane entrance, a local named Wang Erxin, a Daoist priest by profession, has long been addicted to smoking opium. Every night at home, he lies on a couch, indulging in clouds of smoke from dusk till dawn, satisfying his opium cravings. At 3:30 a.m. yesterday, Wang was smoking opium in his upstairs bedroom when he carelessly left a spark in the firewood downstairs (because Wang's wife and mother usually made grass mats, there was a large amount of wheat straw piled downstairs). The fire quickly became uncontrollable and spread to the neighboring houses, affecting Nos. 208 to 204 along the street in Meijia Lane. However, the back doors of these houses, accessed through a small lane, had three rooms with side rooms and two houses. The front door was the wall gate at No. 193 Qiaojia Road and the side door at No. 191, which belonged to the Liao family. When the fire raged, the fire tower rang the alarm. At first, it was mistaken for a fire in Maojia Lane, and fire brigades from various districts rushed their pump trucks to Maojia Lane first. By the time they returned to the fire site, the fire had already spread widely, and it was very difficult to extinguish the fire in the houses at the back. The fire was finally extinguished after about two hours of burning. In this disaster, about twenty buildings were destroyed. The Liao family's three-room, two-side-room buildings were all reduced to ashes. Fortunately, the wall gate and side door buildings in front were not burned. When the fire broke out, all the residents were asleep. Upon hearing the fire alarm, they hastily put on their clothes and fled. None of their belongings could be retrieved, resulting in significant losses. Wang Erxin's wife, Wang Chen, and Wang's two daughters (the elder named San'nan, 17 years old, and the younger named Xiao Si, 11 years old) jumped from the upstairs windows (because the stairs had already been burned through), and were seriously injured in the falls. However, the two-year-old child that the woman was holding was unharmed. The director of the West District Fire Brigade, Mr. Xia, directed the members to help the woman and others into an ambulance and rushed them to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. The most tragic case was that of a madman who was burned to death. A local man named Qian Yanxing, 40 years old, had worked on the railway in his twenties. He was frightened by thieves and became insane. He would bang on tables and chairs all day long, and even wave kitchen knives around. His family feared a major disaster, so they had locked him in a wooden cage in the east wing upstairs behind No. 193 for many years. Because the madman was as strong as an ox, he was also restrained with heavy chains. The madman's younger brother now works at the Xiamen Telegraph Bureau. Living together were the madman's mother, Qian Cai, and his brother's wife. When the fire broke out, his family only cared about their own lives and did not pay attention, so the madman was burned to death. After the fire was extinguished at dawn, the police from the First District, Third Precinct took Wang Erxin's mother, Wang Yuan, to the station for questioning. They also dug out the madman's body, which was charred beyond recognition, with a fractured right leg and both arms in a hugging posture, resembling a dried-out piece of wood. After people cut off the iron chains, they placed the body on a plank door. Shao Meisheng, the local community head from the 20th Precinct, reported to the Local Court requesting an autopsy. The corpse's mother, Qian Cai, also submitted a statement to the court requesting exemption from the autopsy. Her statement roughly stated that she was a local, 62 years old, and the deceased Qian Yanxing was my eldest son, 40 years old this year. He had long suffered from insanity. He was burned to death in this incident due to a neighbor's carelessness, and he was unable to escape. I now wish to prepare the coffin for burial myself and request exemption from the autopsy. The request was approved, and she was instructed to sign a guarantee for the record and quickly arrange for the burial.

One Hundred Thousand Yuan in Ransom Placed Inside a Broken Spittoon 102

▲ Extortionist Detective Reaches Into Spittoon

▲ Just As He Was About to Take the Money, He Was Arrested

▲ Twenty-Two Extortion Letters

▲ Two Criminals Await Sentencing

Wang Xiao'an, residing at No. 477 1/2, Meibai Road, received six threatening letters from gangsters last month. Initially, they attempted to extort 20,000 silver dollars, but later increased the amount to 100,000 dollars. The letters stated that if he was willing to pay the ransom, he should post a note at the lane entrance for contact. Wang reported the letters to the Xinzha Police Station, which instructed him to comply. Several days later, Wang received another letter stating, "We know you sincerely wish to negotiate. Now, take the money to a broken spittoon inside Jingxing Lane on North Henan Road. Someone will come to retrieve it. Otherwise, we will come to pick you up by car." Wang reported to the police, who dispatched detectives to wait. For several days, they did not see the criminals. On September 25th, Wang received another letter instructing him to deliver the ransom to the same location. Wang again reported to the police, who sent Chinese detectives Zhou Guisheng, Bao Tan Ma Zhongrong, Dong Xueyun, Sun Hanying, Yang Feizhang, and others to secretly wait. Not until around 5 a.m. the next morning did they see a criminal arrive, reach into the spittoon, retrieve a paper package, and look delighted. Just as he was about to leave, the detectives apprehended him, took him to the police station, and learned that his name was Chen Xiaobing, from Jiangbei. He was a rickshaw puller at No. 668, Jingxing Lane, North Henan Road. He also confessed that his accomplice was Song Ada, from Tongzhou, hiding inside No. 323 Chongqing Road. The detectives went and apprehended Song, and both were escorted to the Special District Local Court for questioning and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Sun Yuan continued the hearing. Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, stood up and presented the case, stating that during the adjournment, it was discovered that the defendant Chen Xiaobing had also written 22 letters between June 24th and August 25th, sending them to the home of Gu Xingchun, a Ningbo native, at No. 434, Xin Dagulu, in an attempt to extort 20,000 silver dollars. Gu Xingchun has also arrived in court, please question him, and then present the letter as evidence, please investigate. Gu Xingchun also stated that he was a clerk at Luo Maichen Foreign Firm at No. 34 Nanjing Road. After receiving the threatening letters, I reported to the police each time and sent detectives to wait, but they never saw him. When questioned, the defendant Chen Xiaobing admitted that he had written the threatening letters, but Song Ada denied it. After Judge Sun reviewed the evidence, he ordered both defendants to be detained and sentenced next Tuesday.

Wife's Younger Brother Fails to Borrow Money, Assembles Thieves to Rob His Sister's Home 103

▲ The Maid's Shout of "Thieves" Deters the Robbers ▲ Madam Shen Zhang Catches One Thief ▲ The Thief with the Gun is Also Arrested ▲ The Court Adjourns for Further Questioning

Shen Zhongfu, residing at No. 502 Yanping Road, West Shanghai, an employee of the Hua'an Cooperative Life Insurance Company on Jing'an Temple Road, lived with his wife, Zhang. Around 9 a.m. the day before yesterday, Shen had already gone to the company to work. Only Zhang and the maid, Wu Luo, were at home. Suddenly, four thieves broke in. One thief, holding a pistol, threatened to make a sound. Another thief grabbed Zhang by the throat. Just as they were about to begin searching for valuables, the maid stealthily slipped out the back and shouted, "Catch the thieves!" Upon hearing this, the four thieves, without managing to search for anything, fled. The thief with the gun fled out the front door, while the other three thieves escaped through the back door. One of the thieves, named Chen Hongsheng, from Pudong, was chased and caught by Shen Zhang and others at the entrance of the lane. The Chinese Detective Chief of the Gordon Road Police Station, Shen Chongli, and Bao Tan, were patrolling nearby, heard the commotion, and rushed to the scene. They arrested Chen. The thief with the gun was also seen fleeing by a passerby named Zhang, who helped to apprehend him, seizing a pistol with four bullets inside. He handed them over to the Western police. Both thieves were taken to the police station. They were interrogated and identified as Wang A'gen, from Changshu, who confessed that he and Chen Hongsheng were accomplices. They were ordered to be detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Local Court. Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, explained the situation and requested a postponement. The plaintiff, Shen Zhang, also complained that both defendants were present at the scene. Wang held a gun and threatened her, while Chen grabbed her throat and demanded she hand over silver dollars. When questioned, the thieves confessed that the idea was initiated by the plaintiff's younger brother, named A'xiang. A'xiang used to work as a coppersmith at the tram company. Yesterday morning, he asked us to go to his sister's place to borrow money, and gave me a pistol. A'xiang himself was also behind us. When we arrived at the plaintiff's house, we were scared off by the maid's shouting, so we fled and were arrested. Chen confessed that he was being manipulated and didn't know they were going to rob. After reviewing the evidence, Judge Sun Yuan asked the plaintiff's husband, Shen Zhongfu, if he had a brother-in-law named A'xiang. Shen replied that A'xiang was indeed his wife's younger brother, a former worker at the French Concession Tram Company, who usually associated with lowlifes. He had repeatedly asked me to borrow money. I received a call from A'xiang at the company a few days ago, asking to borrow money again. I replied that if he wanted to borrow money, he could come to my house to discuss it, but he did not come. I did not expect this robbery to happen yesterday morning. I request a thorough investigation. After reviewing the evidence, Judge Sun ordered both defendants to be detained and adjourned the hearing for seven days for further investigation.

An Old Man Attempts Suicide in the Huangpu River 106

▲ Fearing No One to Rely On in the Future

▲ Feeling It Better to Die Before His Son

▲ Fortunately Rescued by a Patrol Officer

Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, an old man boarded a ferry from the China Merchants Bureau's Jiangtian Wharf to cross the Huangpu River. Upon reaching the middle of the river, the old man suddenly looked into the water and wept, then attempted to jump into the river to end his life. Quick-eyed passengers grabbed his legs, preventing him from falling into the water. After a short while, when the passengers were not paying attention, he tried to jump into the river again, but was again stopped by the passengers. The passengers strictly monitored him. At one point, they were momentarily distracted, and the old man tried to commit suicide for a third time, but was rescued again. The people, fearing that he would try again, tied the old man up inside the cabin with hemp rope. When the boat arrived at the Pudong Wharf, the boatman untied him and was about to hand him over to the patrol officer when the old man took the opportunity to jump into the river. He was floating up and down in the water. Fortunately, the boatmen made an effort to rescue him from the water and handed him over to the wharf patrol officer, who took him to the Third District General Office. After providing him with dry clothes, the district chief interrogated him. The old man, tearfully, said that his name was Dong Rongqing, 66 years old, from Tongzhou, living on Jin Shenfu Road in the French Concession. His luck had been bad this year. His four sons, the eldest, second, and third, had died one after another from illness. Recently, his youngest son had also fallen seriously ill, moaning in bed. The old man was unable to afford medical treatment for him. Seeing that his son's illness was not improving, if something else were to happen, he would not only have no money to buy a coffin for burial, but he would also have no one to rely on in the future. Thinking of the future, he felt a chill. Therefore, he decided that it would be better to die before his son. As he spoke, he was crying with tears, and his words were very sad. The district chief found his situation extremely pitiful and ordered him sent to the Public Security Bureau to find a way to help him.

The Shanghai art community will host a public banquet for the famous artist Wang Yachen and his wife this afternoon. Mr. Wang studied in Japan for many years, immersed himself in art, and became well-known in Shanghai for more than a decade. The Eight-Cylinder New Buick Car 110

The new 1931 eight-cylinder Buick car is officially on display today. The first batch has arrived in this city and will be officially displayed at the American Buick Motor Company showroom at No. 497 Jing'an Temple Road starting today. The new Buick has many features. Husband and Wife Quarrel Over Career Choice for Son 115

Wife Angrily Swallows Raw Opium, Very Critical Yu Chunsheng, a native of Suzhou residing at No. 317, Fushou Lane, Dalian Bay Road, Hongkou, is over 60 years old and works in the flower carving business. His wife, Zhang, is 49 years old and they have one son and one daughter. The son's name is Pinfa, 16 years old, and the daughter's name is Pinmei, 13 years old. Both are studying at nearby schools. Because the family of four faces difficult living conditions, Yu intends to find a trade for his son Pinfa, who is already grown, to help supplement the family income. Yu intends to have Pinfa learn tailoring, but his wife believes that tailoring has limited prospects and cannot secure his future. She thinks he should study for another year or two and find a better career. However, Yu is unusually stubborn and insists on sending his son to learn the trade from a fellow villager tomorrow. This led to a dispute, almost resulting in physical violence. Neighbors arrived to mediate, and the matter was temporarily resolved. However, the wife remained depressed. She secretly swallowed six jiao worth of raw opium and attempted suicide. Later, someone noticed and took her to Tongren Hospital for treatment. According to the doctor, she had taken too much poison and her life was in danger.

Xia A'xin Killed by Car 116

Xia A'xin, 55 years old, residing at No. 37 Shanzhong Road in the French Concession, was struck by a truck in front of his house at 2:25 PM on the day before yesterday (the 3rd). At 11:30 AM, Judge Zhu arrived at the mortuary and confirmed that the deceased had died from injuries sustained after being hit by a car. After Judge Zhu questioned the defendants and others, he ordered photos to be taken and instructed the family to arrange for the body to be buried after further investigation.

Shanghai Bank Pioneers Sight Draft System 120

The Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, located at No. 9 Ningbo Road in this city, has always aimed to serve society and assist industry and commerce. It has been a pioneer in various new undertakings beneficial to society. For example, travel agencies, traveler's checks, gift certificates, savings deposits, etc., were all first initiated by the bank. To date, the effects have been remarkable, and society has found them convenient. It is recently heard that the bank, in view of the underdevelopment of industry and commerce in our country, due to the lack of popular use of negotiable instruments, has introduced European and American methods and pioneered the sight draft system. According to these measures, when merchants purchase goods, they can open a domestic documentary credit with the bank and give it to the seller. The seller can then issue a draft to the bank, along with the bill of lading, insurance policy, etc., and sell it to another bank. The bank can then accept the draft at the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank. Once the draft has been accepted by the bank, it can be circulated in the market. Once it matures, it can be presented to the bank for payment. Also, a draft issued directly to the buyer by the seller can be discounted at the bank after it has been accepted by the buyer. This measure is of great benefit to the future of industry and commerce in our country. It is heard that the bank has printed detailed regulations, which will be sent upon request.

Henan Native Place Association in Shanghai Sends Telegram Urging Henan People to Govern Henan 121

▲ Requesting the authorities to allocate funds for post-disaster relief

▲ And exempting excessive taxes and special taxes

The Henan Native Place Association in this city, initiated by Fan Zhengbo, Ren Hongjun, Duan Wengong, Wang Zepu, Jia Yusong, Chen Zikuan, Zhu Yaoting, and more than ten others, has already established a preparatory committee. All progress has been quite smooth. More than 600 people have joined the association, showing the need for unity and mutual welfare. The local Henan people in Shanghai have a unanimous demand. It is heard that the association, in view of the fact that the overall situation has been settled and Feng Yuxiang has stepped down, urgently needs to handle post-disaster relief to alleviate the suffering of the people of Henan. It has sent a telegram requesting the authorities to allocate funds for relief and exempt all excessive taxes and miscellaneous taxes. The last paragraph advocates that Henan people govern Henan, in order to ensure that the right people are in charge and that rapid progress is made. The words of the telegram are quite solemn. The following is recorded: To the Central Party Headquarters of the Nationalist Party in Nanjing, the National Government's various ministries, the Party Headquarters of various provinces, the governments of various provinces, the Party Headquarters of various special municipalities, the governments of various municipalities, and all newspapers nationwide: Since the founding of the Republic of China nineteen years ago, wars have been frequent and there has been no peaceful year. In addition to continuous famines, people have been displaced. The old and weak are left in ditches, and the young and strong become bandits. Henan, located in the Central Plains and connecting north and south, has suffered the most from wars. This time, Yan Xishan and Feng Yuxiang waged war and ravaged the entire region even more severely. Wherever artillery fire reached, pavilions were reduced to ruins. Harsh government policies have extracted the marrow from our bones. We cannot seek life, nor can we seek death. This situation is unbearable. Which of us local Henan people in Shanghai does not have parents or siblings? Looking afar at our homeland, our hearts are with our fellow villagers. We only see the tragic atmosphere filling the sky and hear the sounds of moaning filling our ears. Whenever the moon is bright and the wind is clear, we cannot help but look up, beat our chests, and weep blood. Now, fortunately, the overall situation has been settled, the rebellious forces have been eliminated, the war has ended, and peace can be expected. If we can live in peace and work together to sing the praises of prosperity, it will not only be what hundreds of millions of people in Henan are praying for, but also what we local Henan people in Shanghai are longing for day and night. However, although the suffering of war has ended, the wounds of the people have not yet healed. If we do not plan for post-disaster relief, we will only be prolonging our lives. We deeply hope that the governing authorities will consider the suffering of the people and allocate funds for relief, and exempt all excessive taxes and special taxes imposed by the rebel Feng Yuxiang in Henan. We also ask that the various taxes collected by the Central Government be reduced in consideration of the special circumstances, so that the people of Henan can recover and the vitality can be restored. This is the first request that we ask the authorities to adopt when handling post-disaster relief. Moreover, there is something that cannot be left unsaid. Henan Province has repeatedly experienced disasters, and the need for recuperation and recovery cannot be delayed. Only with the right people in charge can we deal with the situation properly. Although Henan people governing Henan may inevitably have some fixed views, we fear that it will be difficult to achieve rapid progress if we only scratch the surface. Therefore, when handling post-disaster relief, we should select people who are familiar with the suffering of the people to take charge of the Henan situation. No one is better than a Henan person. This humble opinion is not intended to cling to localism, but rather to quickly relieve the suffering of the people. We urge the governing authorities to resolutely adopt this proposal and hope that local Henan people and compatriots across the country will unite to support it and respond with sympathy. It will be a great fortune for the people of Henan and a great fortune for the whole country. We send this telegram urgently and cannot express all that we wish to say. We respectfully submit this proposal for your consideration. Respectfully, The Henan Native Place Association in Shanghai.

This Year's Exports to the United States are Sluggish 123

The "Shanghai Evening Post" reports that according to statistics from the US Consulate General, China's national exports to the United States in August decreased by another US$3 million compared to July. The total value was US$5,900,454, while it was US$8,512,373 in July. Compared to US$13,234,854 in the same period last year, it has decreased by more than half. The total value of exports to the United States in the first eight months of this year was US$80,880,896, a decrease of approximately US$36 million compared to US$116,753,371 in the same period last year. This shows that this year's exports to the United States are sluggish.

Shanghai Municipal Council Discusses Adding Parks 124

The "North China Daily News" reported that the proposal to add parks was discussed again at the regular meeting of the Shanghai Municipal Council Board of Directors this Wednesday. According to a letter from the British military commander of the Shanghai area, the landlord of the site of a barracks and training ground rented by a certain British military battalion is about to sell the land. The letter asked if the Shanghai Municipal Council could purchase the land so that it could continue to be rented to the military for stationing. The land was originally in the Shanghai Municipal Council's plan to add parks, so the proposal was discussed together. One director first stated that the Board of Directors had previously resolved that the first priority for adding parks should be in the northern district. The Director-General replied that the area near Jiaozhou Road barracks is developing rapidly, and most of the residents are factory workers. There is currently no public place for recreation, so it is necessary to add a park. The Director-General then sought the opinion of the Acting Chief Accountant, who stated that the land price is approximately 800,000 taels. If it is to be purchased, either other investments this year must be postponed, or the Shanghai Municipal Council must sell its remaining land to allocate funds for this expense. The funds from the sale of the Electricity Department that can be used for investment are only 2.7 million taels. It was previously resolved to use them for investment over four years. The use of funds for the past two years has already been planned and cannot be allocated for the expense of adding parks. As for the remaining land owned by the Shanghai Municipal Council, it is difficult to dispose of it before the expansion plans for various bureaus and departments are decided, determining which to keep and which to sell. After detailed consideration by the directors, opinions varied. Two directors strongly advocated purchasing as soon as possible when an opportunity arises, as the land price will only increase the later it is purchased. Other directors advocated continuing with the original plan. Finally, it was decided to postpone the purchase of land and review the financial situation when preparing the 1931 budget. For the time being, the Director of Public Works was ordered to negotiate a lease renewal with the owner of the barracks to avoid the British military having to move the barracks.

Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau Reforms the Boundary between the French Concession and Zhabei 125

The Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau recently found that the maps and boundaries of the Huajie District and Zhabei District are very inconsistent and urgently need to be reformed to unify them. For the sake of reorganization, the eastern part of the 28th Bao, 3rd Tu, and the southern part of the 4th Tu, and the eastern 18th Tu and 19th Tu of the former Pusong District were划入 (incorporated) into the Huajie District area. Thus, the boundary of the Huajie District will be: east to the boundary line of the Special District, south to Xinpu Huijitang, west to Huo Bilan Road, west to Shangao Pond, and north to the Wusong River. As for the Zhabei District, the land of the 12th Tu of the 27th Bao of the former Zhabei District, its western part is adjacent to the Pusong District, and its eastern part happens to be the confluence of the Wusong River and the Tanzi River, which completely isolates it from the entire topography of the Zhabei District. This Tu has been incorporated into the Pusong District, and the rest remains the old boundary. It is heard that the bureau has drawn the old map Bao boundary map of the two districts, and the corrected map boundary map, and submitted them to the municipal government for record.

Resolution of Dispute over Tobacco and Alcohol Merchants' Treasury Bonds 128

The tobacco and alcohol merchants in the Chinese area of this city were ordered by the Ministry of Finance of the National Government to solicit subscriptions for the 19-year short-term customs treasury bonds. It is heard that the industry has been required to subscribe directly and indirectly several times. Small businesses find it difficult to comply. The Second District of Jiangsu Province Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Office also带徵 (levies along with) the industry, levying 8% of the annual license tax, which is collected along with the winter license collection this year. It has been implemented since the 1st of this month. When the industry went to pay, the office did not issue treasury bonds or receipts. It only stamped the license with a seal indicating that the treasury bonds had been collected. The merchants found this procedure inappropriate. The tobacco兑 (exchange) industry went to the union to request representatives to negotiate. At 8:00 AM yesterday, Chen Kunxian, Yang Bingyi, and other representatives went to the collection office. Director Yang received them. The representatives stated their opinions and were promised compliance. The following was drafted: (1) When paying taxes, 8% of the annual tax should be levied uniformly and collected along with the winter license tax this year, to be paid in full by the 10th of this month. (2) The collected treasury bonds, regardless of amount, should be issued with treasury bond receipts by the collection office, and cancelled with a stamp. (3) Those who paid the license treasury bonds on the 1st, 2nd, and 3rd but did not receive treasury bond receipts can bring their licenses to the office to receive补领 (supplementary) treasury bond receipts. (4) All treasury bond receipts from the collection office should be submitted to the union, which will issue a代存 (temporary storage) receipt to facilitate the aggregation of the total amount and exchange for official treasury bonds from the collection office so that they can be returned. (5) The established method should be communicated by the collection office to the union, and by the union to the industry.
